got to paint fast!&#039;: Local Residents Watch As Capitol Fence Razor Wire Comes Down | DCist","description":"It's the most wonderful time of the year: the Cherry Blossom Festival. ","canonical":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/18\/dc-weekend-events-guide-march-18-cherry-blossom-festival-free-museums\/","featured_image":{"url":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2020\/04\/anthony-delanoix-urUdKCxsTUI-unsplash-1024x683.jpg","width":1024,"height":683},"image":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2018\/08\/dcist-default-og-image-1.png"}},{"ID":4901080,"guid":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/15\/celebrate-cherry-blossom-festival-2021-in-dc\/","title":"16 Ways To Celebrate The Cherry Blossoms In D.C.","content":"<p class=\"p1\">While the pandemic has altered\u00a0the way D.C. typically celebrates its signature springtime blossoms, the 2021 <a href=\"https:\/\/nationalcherryblossomfestival.org\/\"><span class=\"s1\">National Cherry Blossom Festival<\/span><\/a> is still offering plenty of ways to enjoy the flowers, which are expected to reach peak bloom between April 2 and 5.<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\">Running from March 20 to April 11, the festival features a spate of events offered both in-person and virtually. Here are 16 that we\u2019re particularly excited to check out.<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>GO ON A BLOSSOM HUNT: <\/b>The inaugural <a href=\"https:\/\/nationalcherryblossomfestival.org\/art-in-bloom\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Art in Bloom<\/span><\/a> event features 26 giant cherry blossom sculptures painted by local artists. Scout out the sculptures at select outdoor locations throughout D.C., Maryland\u2019s National Harbor, and Virginia\u2019s Aurora Highlands and National Landing neighborhoods. Be sure to read the Sculpture Map and the Art in Bloom Pocket Map (both coming soon) to help chart your quest. (March 20-April 11, FREE)<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>PETAL PORCH PARADE: <\/b>Celebrate the community\u2019s creative cherry blossom spirit with the <a href=\"https:\/\/nationalcherryblossomfestival.org\/event\/porch-parade\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Petal Porch Parade<\/span><\/a>. The parade, held March 20-April 11, features spring-themed porches, yards or windows, each marked on this <a href=\"https:\/\/www.google.com\/maps\/d\/viewer?mid=1eZtd-JMRAidoxrytzkeVEbJ4_evfHma0&amp;ll=38.697483969817384%252C-77.1264583&amp;z=9\"><span class=\"s1\">interactive map<\/span><\/a>. Plan a self-guided Petal Porches tour, and save the date for the Petal Procession on April 10-11, a special blossom-decorated caravan through Petal Porch neighborhoods. (March 20-April 11, FREE)<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>VIRGINIA HIGHLANDS PARK:<\/b> <a href=\"https:\/\/parks.arlingtonva.us\/locations\/virginia-highlands-park\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Virginia Highlands Park<\/span><\/a> in Arlington is hosting several cherry blossom festivities\u2014from kite-flying and outdoor Zumba classes to live music every Friday and Sunday. Check out its\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/aurorahighlands.org\/cherryblossom\/\"><span class=\"s1\">event roster<\/span><\/a> for the full line-up, and register for your choice event. (March 20-April 11, FREE)<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>SELF-GUIDED GARDEN TOURS: <\/b>There are countless beautiful places to enjoy the blossoms, but two gardens in Northern Virginia promise especially astonishing views. Make your way to the 95-acre <a href=\"https:\/\/www.novaparks.com\/parks\/meadowlark-botanical-gardens\"><span class=\"s1\">Meadowlark Botanical Gardens<\/span><\/a>, home to 100+ cherry trees, ornamental display gardens, and the Korean Bell Garden. <a href=\"https:\/\/www.fairfaxcounty.gov\/parks\/green-spring\"><span class=\"s1\">Green Spring Gardens<\/span><\/a>, a national historic site featuring more than 20 thematic demonstration gardens, looks promising, too. <span class=\"s3\">Check with the individual gardens for hours of operation.<\/span> (March 20-April 11, FREE)<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>BOOK IT TO BOOK HILL: <\/b><a href=\"https:\/\/www.georgetowndc.com\/event\/book-hill-in-bloom\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Head to Georgetown<\/span><\/a> to visit (and support!) 25+ small businesses offering cherry blossom seasonal promotions. Sample deals include <a href=\"https:\/\/jacojuiceandtaco.com\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Jaco Juice &amp; Taco Bar\u2019s<\/span><\/a> cherry blossom smoothie; 50% off jewelry at <a href=\"https:\/\/prettychicdc.com\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Pretty Chic<\/span><\/a>; and pink-themed pastries at <a href=\"https:\/\/patisseriepoupon.com\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Patisserie Poupon<\/span><\/a>. Also: Book Hill Park, at Wisconsin Ave. and Reservoir Rd., was selected as an <a href=\"https:\/\/nationalcherryblossomfestival.org\/art-in-bloom\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Art in Bloom<\/span><\/a> sculpture location\u2014so be sure to check it out while it&#8217;s there. (March 20-April 11, FREE)<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>THE BEAUTY OF THE BREW: <\/b>Sake aficionados, rejoice. This season, you can learn even more about sake with the <a href=\"https:\/\/us02web.zoom.us\/webinar\/register\/WN_FIzbpk0ATm6E-pc30R_qUg\"><span class=\"s1\">Beauty of the Brew<\/span><\/a>. Hosted by the <a href=\"https:\/\/sakeassociation.org\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Sake Brewer\u2019s Association of North America<\/span><\/a>, this virtual event debuts SBANA\u2019s <span class=\"s4\">animated video illustrating sake\u2019s unique craft and tradition. Following the film, SBANA member brewers will host a panel discussion on the history of sake and sake-making. <\/span>(March 23 at 7 p.m., FREE)<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><span class=\"s5\"><b>CHERRY-PICK YOUR RESTAURANTS: <\/b><\/span><span class=\"s3\">170+ restaurants in the D.C. area are offering cherry blossom-themed food and drink specials called \u201c<a href=\"https:\/\/nationalcherryblossomfestival.org\/where-to-eat\/\"><span class=\"s6\">Cherry Picks<\/span><\/a><\/span><span class=\"s7\">.\u201d <\/span><span class=\"s8\">Presented in partnership with the Restaurant Association of Metropolitan Washington, Cherry Picks encourage local restaurants to celebrate spring by showcasing their best seasonal menu items. <\/span><span class=\"s3\">Sample spots include <\/span>Belga Caf\u00e9, which is offering a four-course cherry blossom meal, and Bangkok Joe\u2019s, which is touting its Japanese vodka and cherry-infused Blossom Mule. Read the full list of <a href=\"https:\/\/nationalcherryblossomfestival.org\/where-to-eat\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Cherry Picks partners<\/span><\/a>. (Various locations and prices)<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>MAKE A COCKTAIL: <\/b>Fork Tour\u2019s virtual <a href=\"https:\/\/forktours.com\/seasonal-events\/cherry-blossom-cocktails-from-flower-to-fruit\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Cherry Blossom Cocktails tour<\/span><\/a> offers the chance to learn the art of mixology \u2014 cherry blossom-style. Offered Thursday evenings from March 25 to April 15, the tour includes how-to guides for crafting D.C.\u2019s signature cocktail (with a seasonal spin), and a fruit-focused cocktail inspired by a local distillery. Recipes are included so you can re-create drinks after the event. A portion of ticket proceeds go to the local nonprofit Bread for the City. (Thursdays at 7 p.m., March 25-April 15, $30)<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>RENEWAL 2121: <\/b>Artechouse is presenting its fourth\u00a0annual cherry blossom-inspired installation, called<b> <\/b><a href=\"https:\/\/fareharbor.com\/embeds\/book\/artechouse\/items\/281565\/calendar\/2021\/03\/?full-items=yes\"><span class=\"s1\">Renewal 2121<\/span><\/a>. Running now through September 6, the exhibit uses creative technology to depict an industrialized city of the future, with cherry blossoms as a symbol of hope and renewal. Renewal 2121 is presented by Artechouse\u2019s c<span class=\"s3\">reative team, with visual design by Yuya Takeda, music by Mario Hammer and the Lonely Robot, and scenery by Design Foundry. (March 12-September 6, $24 general admission)<\/span><\/p>\n<p class=\"p4\"><span class=\"s10\"><b>LISTEN TO TAIKO: <\/b>On Saturday, March 20, join SAAM for a <a href=\"https:\/\/americanart.si.edu\/events\/virtual-cherry-blossom-celebration-march-20-2021\"><span class=\"s1\">virtual cherry blossom celebration<\/span><\/a> with Japanese t<\/span><span class=\"s3\">aiko drumming by <a href=\"http:\/\/nendaiko.weebly.com\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Nen Daiko<\/span><\/a>. Following the presentation, performers will discuss the history behind their taiko drums, as well as other Japanese percussion instruments like the shekere (a gourd shaker) and\u00a0chappa (hand-held cymbals).<\/span> <span class=\"s3\">The event will wrap-up with a showcase of spring-related artworks in the museum\u2019s collection, guided by SAAM docents. (March 20 at 10 a.m., FREE)<\/span><\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b><span class=\"s10\">JOIN A LECTURE:<\/span> <\/b>Passionate about fashion and design? Check out <a href=\"https:\/\/nationalcherryblossomfestival.org\/event\/renegades-of-fashion-rei-kawakubo-and-yohji-yamamoto\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Fashion in Film: Renegades of Fashion<\/span><\/a> on March 25, a virtual event about the lives and careers of <span class=\"s8\">Rei Kawakubo and Yohji Yamamoto. These two Japanese designers helped revolutionize the fashion industry by abandoning tradition and ushering in a new era of anti-fashion. Prior to the program, watch two 30-minute films about the designers on YouTube, then join Textile Museum curator Lee Talbot for a discussion about their career and influence.<\/span> (March 25 at 6 p.m., FREE)<\/p>\n<p class=\"p5\"><span class=\"s10\"><b>(VIRTUALLY) VISIT THE FREER\/SACKLER: <\/b>The Freer\/Sackler\u2019s <a href=\"https:\/\/asia.si.edu\/events-overview\/performances\/?trumbaEmbed=view%253Devent%2526eventid%253D150827994\"><span class=\"s12\">Look &amp; Listen: Nature in Japanese Art and Music<\/span><\/a><\/span><span class=\"s3\"> virtual event offers an exploration of the gallery\u2019s nature-focused Japanese art, accompanied by the\u00a0<\/span>shakuhachi<span class=\"s3\">\u00a0(bamboo flute). The April 8 event will be guided by curator Frank Feltens, whose recent exhibitions explore Shinto religious art, Hokusai, and modern woodblock prints, and\u00a0Kurahashi\u00a0Yodo\u00a0II, a <\/span>shakuhachi<span class=\"s3\">\u00a0virtuoso hailing from Tokyo. <\/span><span class=\"s10\">(April 8 at 7 p.m., FREE)<\/span><\/p>\n<p class=\"p6\"><span class=\"s3\"><b>PAWS AND PETALS: <\/b>Dogs are an important part of cherry blossom festivities, too. On April 3, tune into the <a href=\"https:\/\/www.instagram.com\/cherryblossfest\/?hl=en\"><span class=\"s1\">National Cherry Blossom Festival\u2019s Instagram<\/span><\/a> for the Paws and Petals Parade, featuring pups in their finest spring and cherry blossom attire. Interested in joining? Submit a 10-second video of your dressed-up pup by March 24. <a href=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/playlist?list=PLce0GP0YDD01qGlU40Li9UMWnrUmhJ-XU\"><span class=\"s1\">Check out this video<\/span><\/a> for an example of a best practice submission.<b> <\/b><\/span><span class=\"s10\">(April 3, FREE)<\/span><\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>SAKURA MATSURI:<\/b> On April 3 from 12 p.m. to 3 p.m., celebrate the beauty and fun of cherry blossom season with the <a href=\"https:\/\/jaswdc.org\/events\/sakura-matsuri-virtual-community-gathering\/1617451200\/1617462000\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Sakura Matsuri<\/span><\/a>. Hosted by the Japan-America Society of Washington, D.C., this virtual gathering will feature stage performances and the opportunity to interact with Sakura Matsuri exhibitors, vendors, and participants. More info and registration will be available soon. (April 3 at 12 p.m., FREE)<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>SAKURA SUNDAYS:<\/b> Find your inner peace at the National Harbor\u2019s <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nationalharbor.com\/cherryblossom\/sakura-sundays\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Sakura Sundays<\/span><\/a>, featuring free outdoor yoga and meditation, and a Zen sand garden. <a href=\"https:\/\/caricature-dc.com\/\"><span class=\"s1\">Dana Verkouteren<\/span><\/a>, a sand artist, professional courtroom sketch artist, and caricaturist will create a new garden each Sunday at the Harbor\u2019s Awakening Beach. Classes and demonstrations are held Sundays from March 21 through April 11. (March 21-April 11, FREE)<\/p>\n<p class=\"p6\"><span class=\"s3\"><b>PEEP THE BLOOM CAM:<\/b> Not able to catch the peak bloom April 2-5 in person? Tune into the National Park Service\u2019s <a href=\"https:\/\/nationalcherryblossomfestival.org\/bloom-watch\/\"><span class=\"s1\">BloomCam<\/span><\/a>, offering 24\/7, real-time views<\/span><span class=\"s13\"> of the Cherry Trees lining the Tidal Basin<\/span><span class=\"s10\">. <\/span><span class=\"s3\">Last year, the webcam was viewed more than 750,000 times by people in <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/01\/dc-cherry-blossom-festival-peak-bloom-tidal-basin\/\"><span class=\"s1\">more than 160 countries<\/span><\/a>. You would have seen people talking about the importance of the $1,400 stimulus checks,&#8221; says Byrne, adding that there likely would have been artwork installed on the Capitol lawn, too.<\/p>\n<p>But\u00a0demonstrators couldn&#8217;t get that close.\u00a0Instead, officials offered up the far side of Third Street, on the National Mall and across the street from the Capitol complex. It &#8220;didn&#8217;t have the sight and sound of electeds, [who] need to see the public. They&#8217;ve been in a very cloistered environment since January 7,&#8221; Byrne says.<\/p>\n<p>Ever since pro-Trump insurrectionists stormed the U.S. Capitol on January 6, more than three miles of tall fences topped with razor wire have surrounded the Capitol complex, much to the <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/02\/17\/capitol-hill-residents-are-leading-the-fight-against-fence-around-congress\/\">chagrin and inconvenience of nearby residents.<\/a>\u00a0Nearly 2,300 <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/04\/capitol-police-national-guard-stay-d-c-two-more-months\/\">National Guard troops will remain<\/a> in the District to help provide security at the Capitol until May 23.<\/p>\n<p>But those aren&#8217;t the only security measures keeping the public out. Capitol Police has stopped issuing <a href=\"https:\/\/www.uscp.gov\/sites\/uscapitolpolice.house.gov\/files\/wysiwyg_uploaded\/U.S.%20Capitol%20Grounds%20Demonstration%20Area%20Map.pdf\">permits for special events on the grounds<\/a> ever since the insurrection, preventing peaceful protesters from making their voices heard.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Due to access restrictions, the permitting process is currently on hold,&#8221; a department spokesperson said over email.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;All of the public that normally does organizing has been shut out [of the Capitol] because of the police&#8217;s failure to respond to known threats,&#8221; says Byrne, referring to <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/01\/26\/us-capitol-police-armed-threats-insurrection-dc-security\/\">law enforcement&#8217;s inadequate preparation<\/a>\u00a0for January 6.<\/p>\n<p>The U.S. Capitol is one of the biggest stages for protest in the city.\u00a0 Advocates and organizers say that choking off the public&#8217;s access has a negative impact on free speech and affects their ability to bring public attention to their causes.<\/p>\n<p>There are a lot of reasons why activists favor the Capitol for their demonstrations. Some of them are logistical: the buildings are filled with lawmakers to persuade (or who may even swing by to show their support), as well as members of the national media, who can get out a group&#8217;s message with a single tweeted photo.<\/p>\n<p>Those planning civil disobedience in the District often plan those actions at the U.S. Capitol. While D.C. police has a policy stating officers won&#8217;t arrest peaceful protesters, the Capitol Police does not&#8212;that means sit-ins at any of the buildings at the complex often\u00a0lead to hundreds of arrests, bringing headlines and attention to causes like the <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/18\/12\/10\/capitol-police-arrest-nearly-140-protesters-demanding-green-new-deal\/\">Green New Deal<\/a> or <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/18\/06\/28\/hundreds-of-women-are-risking-arres\/\">ending family detention<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>And then, of course, there&#8217;s the symbolic value &#8212; it&#8217;s the architectural embodiment of American democracy. The U.S. Capitol was designed to be open, as was the <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/20\/06\/05\/d-c-s-street-plan-is-a-monument-to-democracy\/\">street plan leading the way<\/a> to the historic building.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;It&#8217;s a celebration of democracy to have people up there protesting,&#8221; says Congressman Don Beyer (D-Va). &#8220;I&#8217;ve always thought that it was a good thing when people show up to speak on Capitol Hill, regardless of where they are on the ideological spectrum &#8212; it shows great civic engagement.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Robby Diesu, a longtime organizer for large-scale protests, says that the purpose of these demonstrations isn&#8217;t necessarily to change a lawmaker&#8217;s mind in that moment, but instead to influence the public perception of an issue over time.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;A member of Congress seeing people having a rally outside the Capitol when they&#8217;re going to vote may not change their mind there,&#8221; he says, but that&#8217;s not the intention. &#8220;Thinking about the long term of building political power, people demonstrating over a period of time helps shift the narrative.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Before the pandemic shut down the complex&#8217;s buildings to visitors, anyone could enter to petition their lawmakers or watch proceedings as long as they went through a metal detector. Special permits weren&#8217;t required for groups of fewer than 20 people.<\/p>\n<p>Until January 6, Capitol Police continued to issue special events permits for outdoor locations on the grounds, with a cap of 50 participants. (Another change: before the pandemic, people could only request a permit in person or via a fax machine. The office started accepting email requests last spring.)<\/p>\n<p>Organizers continued to hold events and set up displays on the Capitol lawn. Progressive advocacy groups, unions, and healthcare organizations placed more than <a href=\"https:\/\/www.businessinsider.com\/photos-healthcare-workers-us-capitol-lawn-ppe-2020-4#as-of-mid-april-more-than-9200-healthcare-workers-have-been-infected-by-the-coronavirus-which-causes-a-respiratory-illness-known-as-covid-19-1\">1,000 signs depicting frontline healthcare workers<\/a> in April, calling on the government to provide them with personal protective equipment. In July, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cbsnews.com\/news\/nurses-shoes-died-coronavirus-capitol-lawn-164-health-care-workers-pandemic\/\">National Nurses United placed 164 pairs of shoes<\/a>\u00a0on the lawn, to represent the nurses who had died of COVID-19 at the time.<\/p>\n<p>Demonstrations like these aren&#8217;t allowed right now, and it&#8217;s unclear when they&#8217;ll be possible again.<\/p>\n<p>Capitol Police <a href=\"https:\/\/www.uscp.gov\/media-center\/press-releases\/uscp-statement-security-changes-us-capitol\">announced on Monday<\/a> that it would &#8220;continue to improve access around the U.S. Capitol&#8221; in the coming week but would &#8220;not provide a detailed timeline of specific, future changes,&#8221; citing security. Already, the <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/15\/us-capitol-police-plan-to-remove-fencing-email-shows\/\">fencing has shrunk<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>While Acting Chief Yogananda Pittman has <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/01\/28\/capitol-police-chief-fence-us-capitol-dc-mayor\/\">called for permanent perimeter fencing<\/a>, the department&#8217;s statement this week referred to the current infrastructure as &#8220;temporary.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Beyer, like the vast majority of officials representing the region, opposes permanent fencing around the Capitol complex. &#8220;I haven&#8217;t met anybody who likes it,&#8221; he says. &#8220;It is a walling off of the elected representatives from the people, and that&#8217;s a bad symbol.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>He&#8217;s also skeptical that permanent fencing would make the complex more secure. &#8220;You can make a pretty good argument that it wasn&#8217;t primarily the lack of defensive fortifications, but rather of the diminished imagination on the part of the U.S. Capitol Police leadership&#8221; and <strong>&#8220;<\/strong>absence of coordination between different law enforcement,&#8221; says Beyer. &#8220;It\u00a0would be terrible to take this one insurrection &#8230; and generalize from that to a need to shut down the Capitol<b> <\/b>on those grounds on a permanent basis.&#8221;\u00a0<em>\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<p>Monica Hopkins, the executive director of the D.C. American Civil Liberties Union, wants to know when the fences are coming down.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;What we know here in District of Columbia is once you put up sort of security barriers, it&#8217;s really difficult to take them down. The longer you leave them up, it just becomes part of the architecture,&#8221; she says, adding that the longer the fences remain, the more of a First Amendment issue it could become.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;As the vaccine rolls out, as we go back to quote unquote normal, and people actually can start gathering in crowds, we live in the First Amendment epicenter,&#8221; says Hopkins. &#8220;What will that [fence] mean for people actually coming to D.C. to make their voices heard?&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>A Capitol Police spokesperson says over email that &#8220;as the security posture continues to be modified to facilitate greater access to the Complex, the Department anticipates that permitting will soon be restored within the confines of recommended COVID restrictions.&#8221;<\/p>\n","paginatedContent":[],"excerpt":"<p>Capitol Police hasn&#8217;t issued any special event permits since January 6. <\/p>\n","permalink":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/19\/increased-security-capitol-grounds-fencing-protests\/","currentSlug":"increased-security-capitol-grounds-fencing-protests","created":"2021-03-19T15:09:36","modified":"2021-03-19T15:09:36","time":"Mar 19","timestamp":1616166576,"timestampGMT":1616180976,"imageData":{"caption":"<p>Security fencing surrounding the Capitol area in January. ","canonical":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/19\/increased-security-capitol-grounds-fencing-protests\/","featured_image":{"url":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/210113_CapitolSecurity_Turner_10-1024x683.jpg","width":1024,"height":683},"image":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2018\/08\/dcist-default-og-image-1.png"}},{"ID":4901732,"guid":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/19\/slow-response-to-racism-at-northern-virginia-football-game\/","title":"Parents Decry Slow Response To Racist Incident At Northern Virginia High School Football Game","content":"<p>Local parents say they are angry that it took a full two weeks before school officials in Northern Virginia publicly acknowledged an incident at a high school football game in which Black students were allegedly spit on and called the N-word.<\/p>\n<p>It happened on March 5 at a football game between Wakefield High School, in Arlington, and Marshall High School, in Fairfax County. Lydia Hatcher, a Wakefield parent, was at the game to see her son Lukai play.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;I&#8217;m watching all of this happen, I am seeing my son&#8217;s body language,&#8221; recalls Hatcher.\u00a0&#8220;My son was immediately a target of a player who I later found out was the same player who targeted him on the basketball court as well.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Hatcher says her son was spit on by the Marshall player, and also called &#8220;boy&#8221; and the &#8220;N-word&#8221; during the game.\u00a0&#8220;Spitting is an assault, in a pandemic \u2014 it&#8217;s a deadly assault, actually,&#8221; says Hatcher.<\/p>\n<p>The incident only became public this week, when students took to social media to talk about it.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Me and my teammates were called racial slurs, taunted, and even spit on by Marshall players. We also experienced unfair treatment by each of the refs and were harassed from the sidelines by coaches and Marshall parents,&#8221; <a href=\"https:\/\/www.instagram.com\/p\/CMiagTVLZhk\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">wrote Lukai Hatcher<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>At the end of the game a fight broke out, one that Wakefield players and parents say was\u00a0instigated by Marshall students. Players from both teams were suspended for three games.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;This isn&#8217;t new and enough is enough! We should not be punished for defending ourselves and each other,&#8221; wrote Lukai Hatcher.<\/p>\n<p>Whytni Kernodle, president of the group Black Parents of Arlington, says Arlington Public Schools officials should not have waited until the incident blew up on social media to address it.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;When things like this happen, people need to know about it,&#8221; Kernodle says.\u00a0&#8220;These are the things that my son and his friends have been talking about for almost two weeks. That&#8217;s completely and utterly inappropriate, and a failure on the part of the administration and the principal.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Students have started <a href=\"https:\/\/www.change.org\/p\/aps-playfairnow?redirect=false\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">an online petition<\/a> calling for an apology from Marshall High School, among other measures. It has garnered more than 4,000 signatures.<\/p>\n<p>Arlington Public Schools officials released statements after the students posted on social media, deploring what happened at the game. &#8220;The blatant acts of racism and disrespect towards the Wakefield players are completely unacceptable and will not be tolerated,&#8221; wrote superintendent\u00a0Francisco Dur\u00e1n, in <a href=\"https:\/\/www.apsva.us\/post\/a-message-from-the-superintendent-5\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a letter to families<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Dur\u00e1n said Arlington officials had been in contact with officials in Fairfax and at the Virginia High School League, which referees games. Dur\u00e1n wrote that league officials failed to act during the game, &#8220;after repeated attempts by players and coaches to alert them,&#8221; to the racist behavior.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;This lack of action by officials as players were spat upon and called racist slurs allowed the situation to escalate, resulting in the suspension of three of our players,&#8221; wrote Dur\u00e1n.<\/p>\n<p>Chris Willmore, Wakefield&#8217;s principal, also wrote to parents, and outlined steps school leaders were taking.\u00a0\u00a0&#8220;All coaches have been instructed to leave the field\/court immediately if our student-athletes are subject to racist, bigoted behaviors. Our student-athletes will not be put into a position like this again,&#8221; <a href=\"https:\/\/www.apsva.us\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Community-Message-regarding-Incident-at-Marshall-1.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">wrote Willmore<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Willmore also said he was calling on the Virginia High School League &#8220;to take concrete steps to address racism and bigotry with their staff,&#8221; and said he had written VHSL leaders describing additional incidents in past years. Willmore said that as for the suspensions of Wakefield students, an appeal had already reduced the suspensions from three games for each player to one game, and &#8220;VHSL guidelines do not permit eliminating the suspensions entirely.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Fairfax County Public Schools conducted a &#8220;thorough investigation&#8221; into the incident, according to a statement from spokesperson Lucy Caldwell. &#8220;FCPS does not accept acts of intolerance. We have expectations of behavior in our students and staff; allegations such as these are taken seriously,&#8221; wrote Caldwell.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The investigation was extensive and involved VHSL, officials, staff, players and families \u2014 from both teams.&#8221; Caldwell said that all parties were working &#8220;to develop a plan for restorative justice.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>A spokesperson for VHSL said he couldn&#8217;t comment on the specifics of the incident due to privacy concerns of those involved. However, VHSL did review video of the game after learning of the racist incidents,\u00a0said Mike McCall in an emailed statement.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The VHSL membership has mandated that the use of any racial slurs would not be tolerated and adopted policy that any use of inappropriate terms would be an ejection. The VHSL has penalties in place for violations,&#8221; wrote McCall.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The VHSL continues to make a point of major emphasis with our coaches and official associations that there is no tolerance for racially charged words or actions and strongly condemns racial slurs of any kind,&#8221; he continued.<\/p>\n<p>But Whytni Kernodle isn&#8217;t satisfied with the delayed response from officials.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;It goes into that whole &#8216;white silence equals violence&#8217; \u2014 pretending that things don&#8217;t exist or leaving them out of notice of the community is perpetuating it,&#8221; she says.\u00a0&#8220;What we should not be doing is needing Black children to lead the charge against racism, and anti-Black racism specifically.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>APS officials say they&#8217;ve had conversations with the families involved in the incident. But Lydia Hatcher says she hasn&#8217;t been contacted. &#8220;The spin that&#8217;s being put on what has been done is incorrect, and that enrages me on top of being enraged by the incident,&#8221; Hatcher says.<\/p>\n<p>Hatcher says that as far as she knows, it&#8217;s the first time her son has experienced such overt racism during a game. &#8220;This is one of the things that Black parents work so hard to protect their kids from. When they&#8217;re in an environment that&#8217;s controlled by adults who are supposed to protect them, they have \u2014 my son has been failed.&#8221;<\/p>\n","paginatedContent":[],"excerpt":"<p>Black students say they were called &#8220;boy&#8221; and the &#8220;N-word&#8221; during a football game, but parents didn&#8217;t find out It assists with preventative health, housing, immigration services and aid for victims of sexual violence. Ruby Corado, the prominent transgender activist who opened the organization in 2012 and currently serves as director, <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/01\/05\/ruby-corado-stepping-down-casa-ruby-dc\/\">announced in January<\/a> that she will step down within the next two years. This facility in historic Anacostia <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/19\/09\/20\/two-new-lgbtq-services-centers-open-in-southeast\/\">opened in August 2019<\/a>, joining a 24\/7 center in Shepherd Park.<\/p>\n<p>The <a href=\"https:\/\/www.washingtonblade.com\/2021\/03\/18\/casa-ruby-wellness-center-burglarized\/\">Washington Blade first reported<\/a> on the burglary this week.<\/p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"500\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Our center in S.E DC Was burglarized, hoping to find some answers soon! <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/uTLKfeqI9p\">https:\/\/t.co\/uTLKfeqI9p<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Casa Ruby (@CasaRubyDC) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/CasaRubyDC\/status\/1372899582158454792?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 19, 2021<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/p>\n<p>Kisha Allure, a case manager, told the Blade that the break-in happened while she was gone, but called police when she returned. Eytan","source_url":"https:\/\/www.flickr.com\/photos\/taedc\/12784750434\/in\/photolist-ktKbTC-ktGzZ2-ktGTae-ktGNND-ktGKBP-ktGNdF-ktGU5v-ktJzx7-ktJhDs-ktGCpc-ktGFzv-ktJjZQ-ktGGgk-ktGDeP-ktJsBJ-UqSsmC-V1YDUr-26bqZxN-pRu2sf-SMVzhX-24wrNWY-UPfamk-RJRNzA-kJ3s8s-ktJyVq-Rpkq5w-SXLSK5-2gxKucH-SVF1Xm-Spom3U-SMC7GN-SL3a2b-SZPRER-pRAQut-SVF5XL-Q97FNY-q6KQ1s-RKShTx-RKhZUP-pc3WEm-Spok8h-pRAPvp-q93hLg-pRt819-q8YY8s-pchkAz-pRt96W-q93iDt-pRC8bk-T2HfsH"},"postMeta":{"showDCistStoryAppeal":true,"person":"4866717","secondaryImage":{"type":"","data":""},"titleOverride":false,"urlOrigin":false},"audio":{"postPermalink":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/19\/casa-ruby-wellness-center-southeast-dc-burglary\/"},"beat":"News","beatSlug":"news","slug":{"name":"News","permalink":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/beat\/news\/","categoryName":"","providerClass":"provider-wamu","flagSlug":"","flagText":"","nameOverride":false,"showTimestamp":false},"promoted":"","headMeta":{"title":"&#039;I&#039;ve got to paint fast!&#039;: Local Residents Watch As Capitol Fence Razor Wire Comes Down | DCist","description":"Police are looking for a suspect and are reviewing cameras in the area. ","canonical":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/19\/casa-ruby-wellness-center-southeast-dc-burglary\/","featured_image":{"url":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/12784750434_2446689e05_k-1024x575.jpg","width":1024,"height":575},"image":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2018\/08\/dcist-default-og-image-1.png"}},{"ID":4901733,"guid":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/19\/motel-shelter-program-dhs-unhoused-medically-vulnerable-residents\/","title":"D.C. Hesitates To Expand Hotel Shelter Program For Medically Vulnerable Residents, As Waitlist Grows","content":"<p>After 15 years bouncing between periodic stays in shelters and living outside, 60-year-old Maurice Ceasar moved into a D.C. hotel last March. Every day, he had access to meals, on-site medical care, and a bathroom \u2014 plus a room of his own, where he could safely avoid contracting the coronavirus that was sweeping through the city.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cFor me, it was like a dream come true,\u201d says Ceasar, who has cardiovascular conditions that place him at a high risk of falling ill if he contracts COVID-19. \u201cI needed the support, I needed the people, and they were there for me.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Ceasar stayed for nearly seven months at the Fairfield Inn on New York Avenue NE, and later at the nearby Hotel Aboretum on Bladensburg Road, two of three hotels the city is leasing to house residents experiencing homelessness during the pandemic.<\/p>\n<p>In March, as the coronavirus swept through the city \u2014 and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.washingtonpost.com\/local\/hundreds-of-dcs-homeless-have-tested-positive-for-coronavirus-as-shelters-try-to-avoid-spread\/2020\/05\/08\/2bcfc03c-8fb4-11ea-8df0-ee33c3f5b0d6_story.html\">its homeless shelters <\/a>\u2014 the Department of Human Services began renting hotel rooms to quarantine and isolate residents experiencing homelessness that had tested positive for the virus, or had come into close contact with an individual who had contracted COVID-19. DHS was leasing rooms for <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/20\/04\/23\/more-than-200-residents-experiencing-homelessness-are-in-quarantine-at-five-d-c-hotels\/\">more than 200 people<\/a> at five hotels for self-quarantining by April, including one site for medically vulnerable residents that had not contracted the virus, but would be at high-risk of serious illness.<\/p>\n<p>In May, DHS expanded that preventative hotel housing for D.C.\u2019s most at-risk unhoused residents through a program called Pandemic Emergency Program for Medically Vulnerable Individuals, which is what Ceasar used to receive shelter. The agency leased 193 rooms at the Holiday Inn on Rhode Island Avenue NW, and in October, added 115 rooms to house medically vulnerable residents at the Fairfield Inn.<\/p>\n<p>Unlike DHS\u2019 previous shelter-hotel model, in which residents reported <a href=\"https:\/\/washingtoncitypaper.com\/article\/185391\/life-inside-dcs-motel-homeless-shelters\/\">poor conditions and alleged abuse by contractors, r<\/a>eviews of the PEP-V program have been markedly positive \u2014 the hotels provide on-site medical care through Unity Health, mental health services, and case management. Also unlike other shelter programs, the federal government will reimburse 100% of the costs to lease the hotels.<\/p>\n<p>And in the months since the program began, demand for it has boomed.<\/p>\n<p>The three hotels \u2014 the Fairfield Inn, Holiday Inn, Hotel Arboretum \u2014 currently house a total of 627 residents, according to DHS\u2019 most recent count, maxing out capacity even as some residents double-up in rooms. Of those current residents, 215 <a href=\"https:\/\/storymaps.arcgis.com\/stories\/b8c0374078644c5298ad2b6b8dfbf751\">have been matched<\/a> to permanent housing resources but have not yet moved out, and 182 people have moved into permanent supportive housing since the program began last March. (No residents are forced to leave until they find another housing solution, or choose to exit voluntarily.)<\/p>\n<p>But as the waitlist for PEP-V grows to more than 600 \u2014 nearly matching the number of people in the program \u2014 placements out of hotels into permanent housing are not meeting the pace of demand to get in. And despite widespread support for the program, the hundreds of unhoused people on a waiting list for it, and a pool of federal dollars available to fund the program, D.C. has not made plans to expand PEP-V into a fourth hotel.<\/p>\n<p>Advocates for the homeless, along with members of the D.C. Council, are calling on DHS to place the hundreds currently depending on the program into more permanent spaces, and to open a fourth hotel to accommodate the waitlist \u2014 warning that, if the agency chooses not to, it could jeopardize the steps the D.C. has already taken toward <a href=\"https:\/\/www.washingtonpost.com\/local\/dc-politics\/dc-family-homeless\/2021\/03\/13\/41c74204-4b9b-11eb-a9f4-0e668b9772ba_story.html\">eliminating homelessness<\/a> during the pandemic.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cTo linger off and not support [PEP-V] would be a disaster for a lot of people, for minorities \u2014 which are in Washington D.C, living in poverty, living on the streets,\u201d Ceasar says.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIt&#8217;s almost certain that many of the people currently [in PEP-V housing] are going to return to homelessness after the public health emergency is over,\u201d says Karen Cunningham, the executive director of Everyone Home DC, a nonprofit that connects residents experiencing homelessness with housing and other wrap-around services. \u201cNow, the worst case scenario is that we don&#8217;t get more PEP-V, and we don&#8217;t get more people into housing.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Despite the progress the city has made in vaccinating residents living in congregate shelters, <a href=\"https:\/\/storymaps.arcgis.com\/stories\/b8c0374078644c5298ad2b6b8dfbf751\">administering more than 2,600 doses as of March 16<\/a>, the virus has still <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/20\/10\/15\/dc-homelessness-pandemic-covid19-shelter\/\">disproportionately impacted<\/a> Washingtonians experiencing homelessness. Cunningham says that seeing how well the PEP-V program has worked for its participants \u2014 not only in protecting them from COVID-19, but also providing privacy and a path to permanent housing \u2014 the city should use that lesson going forward to expand PEP-V.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIt\u2019s showing that when we offer people the right kind of housing with a great degree of privacy that they need, some on-site support, that they can really thrive, just like they do in permanent supportive housing,\u201d Cunningham says. \u201cIt\u2019s more dignified than going into these huge congregate settings.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>A majority of the funding for the PEP-V and quarantine housing sites came from the federal CARES Act passed in March 2020, while D.C. covered 25% of the costs. But President Joe Biden<a href=\"https:\/\/www.fema.gov\/press-release\/20210203\/fema-statement-100-cost-share\"> issued an executive order <\/a>last month requiring FEMA to fully reimburse any money spent by local and state governments on hotel programs for unhoused residents during the pandemic. The funds will run through Sept. 30, but will also apply retroactively to any state or local money invested in the programs so far that was not previously eligible for federal funding \u2014 an avenue advocates are calling on DHS to utilize to move residents out of congregate shelters.<\/p>\n<p>According to the District\u2019s Homeland Security and Emergency Management Agency, which oversees the billing to FEMA, the city has requested a federal reimbursement of $17 million for the PEP-V and quarantine housing programs. FEMA has approved $11.9 of that request so far, and according to HSEMA and DHS, the city expects to receive another $11 million from FEMA for costs related to non-congregate shelters \u2014 but DHS wouldn\u2019t confirm to DCist\/WAMU if it plans to expand the program into a fourth hotel.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWith the announcement by the Biden administration that 100% of cost for these hotels will be reimbursed, we expected DHS to expand the program,\u201d said Amber Harding, an attorney with the Washington Legal Clinic for the Homelesses, during the D.C. Council\u2019s annual performance oversight hearing of DHS. \u201cThis has not happened&#8230;D.C. must expand PEP-V immediately to prevent further loss of life, and to accommodate every high risk person experiencing homelessness.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>In an interview with DCist, Zeilinger says that the cost and logistics of opening another PEP-V hotel is cumbersome \u2013 even with significant federal assistance \u2013 since some PEP-V services, like case management and mental health counselling, aren\u2019t eligible for reimbursement from FEMA. DHS could not tell DCist how much the program has cost the city in the past year, which is likely higher than what will be reimbursed by the federal government.<\/p>\n<p>Zeilinger pegs the cost of housing one resident in a PEP-V hotel for one month at roughly $12,800, given the costs of staffing, medical care, and other wrap-around services. She also says the agency is also weighing the need to build out other services, like expanding the vaccine rollout for residents experiencing homelessness, and placing the hundreds of people currently living in PEP-V in permanent housing.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe want to make sure we&#8217;re keeping our energy and effort on our long term solutions, as well as what we need to do in the immediate to protect people&#8217;s health,\u201d Zeilinger says. \u201cAnd that does not mean we&#8217;re not continuing to consider in addition to [long term solutions] that we should be expanding into another hotel, but we want to make sure that we are focused on the right things.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>But others have looked towards the recent passage of the American Rescue Plan to bolster the city\u2019s housing efforts, and costs that might not be reimbursed by the recent FEMA order. The <a href=\"https:\/\/www.whitehouse.gov\/briefing-room\/legislation\/2021\/01\/20\/president-biden-announces-american-rescue-plan\/\">latest relief package<\/a> includes $5 billion for states and localities to address homelessness, including funding to purchase hotels that are currently leased out in a PEP-V-like program.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThere&#8217;s a ton of federal money coming down from the two recent federal bills that we haven&#8217;t spent yet,\u201d Harding says. \u201cThere&#8217;s [Community Development Block Grant] funds, and then there&#8217;s coronavirus relief funds&#8230;if we haven&#8217;t spent all that yet, any of that money can be used to pay for supportive services in non-congregate shelter.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Harding also says that the <a href=\"https:\/\/cfo.dc.gov\/page\/emergency-and-contingency-cash-reserve-fund-status-reports\">city\u2019s reserves<\/a> could be a stream of revenue for continuing PEP-V, and covering some of the wrap-around services costs related to PEP-V that the federal government may not reimburse . When federal funding for business relief ran out last summer, the city tapped into its contingency reserves to<a href=\"https:\/\/www.bizjournals.com\/washington\/news\/2020\/11\/18\/dc-business-relief-grants-new-coronavirus.html\"> fund $80 million <\/a>in grants for struggling businesses.<\/p>\n<p>In mid-February of this year, Ward 1 Councilmember and chair of the Committee on Human Services Brianne Nadeau called on Mayor Muriel Bowser to allocate a portion of the fiscal year 2022 budget to <a href=\"https:\/\/brianneknadeau.com\/updates\/update\/councilmember-brianne-k-nadeau-sends-letter-fy22-budget-mayor-bowser\">purchase the hotels<\/a> for short-term PEP-V housing and longer term permanent supportive housing. In a<a href=\"https:\/\/mcusercontent.com\/467cc2381663d8fde782cd361\/files\/4b4d7dc6-27bb-4fcc-ae7f-641dd98bb436\/CM_McDuffie_Budget_Letter_FY22_.pdf?mc_cid=4f62872c0e&amp;mc_eid=UNIQID\"> similar letter to the mayor<\/a>, Ward 5 Councilmember Kenyan McDuffie requested that the city invest $140 million in the next budget to purchase and convert the Washington Marriott Wardman Park Hotel into an affordable and permanent supportive housing site.<\/p>\n<p>The Fair Budget Coalition, a progressive advocacy and policy group, has issued the same recommendations, asking that Bowser purchase struggling hotels and convert them into either non-congregate emergency or permanent housing. (Bowser will present her proposed 2022 budget at the end of this month.)<\/p>\n<p>\u201cDuring the pandemic, we have seen that people are more likely to die of COVID-19 in overcrowded, congregate shelters,\u201d reads the FBC\u2019s<a href=\"https:\/\/drive.google.com\/file\/d\/1v8yHEG7tImgRRhWg4Bl3CnoqwhFpFvVu\/view\"> latest fiscal year 2022 report.<\/a> \u201cD.C. needs safe, humane shelter options and deeply affordable housing to prevent sickness, death, and trauma.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The demands for converted hotel space aren\u2019t unique; last year, California began <a href=\"https:\/\/www.pewtrusts.org\/en\/research-and-analysis\/blogs\/stateline\/2020\/12\/04\/prompted-by-pandemic-some-states-buy-hotels-for-the-homeless\">purchasing entire hotels<\/a> when the federal emergency dollars that funded rented hotel rooms ran out, and the state set aside more than $800 million to convert 6,055 hotel units into housing. Oregon took a <a href=\"https:\/\/www.oregonlive.com\/news\/2020\/10\/oregon-lawmakers-approve-30-million-to-purchase-motels-and-hotels-as-shelters-in-wildfire-areas-zero-for-the-rest-of-the-state.html#:~:text=Oregon%20lawmakers%20voted%20on%20Friday,homes%20burned%20in%20recent%20wildfires.\">similar approach<\/a>, purchasing hotels for emergency, transitional, and permanent housing options that will extend beyond the pandemic\u2019s end.<\/p>\n<p>Zeilinger says DHS has not made any decisions regarding the future of PEP-V hotels yet, but acknowledged the city\u2019s ability to purchase a commercial space for housing purposes in the new federal relief package.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe know there&#8217;s some opportunities potentially to acquire buildings that can be used for this purpose, and to subsidize those buildings to make more housing affordable for people at the very lowest income spectrum to, which then allows us to support people to exit homelessness without such deep housing subsidies, and it\u2019s also just important in terms of homelessness prevention,\u201d Zeilinger says, adding that purchasing a building for the purposes of converting it into housing would not be an immediate solution for PEP-V residents, but a longer-term investment.<\/p>\n<p>According to Zeilinger, the city is also facing a shortage of permanent housing solutions for those residents currently living in the program \u2014 meaning that when it ends, some would likely return to congregate shelters.<\/p>\n<p>For PEP-V participants like Maurice Ceasar, living in the hotel gave him a network of around-the-clock support that he says he wouldn\u2019t have had access to otherwise \u2014 like on-site medical care and regular check-ins with providers \u2014 that some residents could lose, should they exit the program without a match to another housing option.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThey feed you, they give you the opportunity to wash, they give you the opportunity to talk and communicate with programs like [MBI Health Services] and Unity Health Care,\u201d Ceasar says. \u201cThere were a lot of great things inside that place [and the program] is really needed today.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>While Zeilinger says there\u2019s no end date on the program yet since no residents are forced to leave until they are placed into housing or they voluntarily exit on their own, the future of the program still remains uncertain for DHS.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI think one thing we know is that we don&#8217;t know how long [PEP-V] is going to last,\u201d Zeilinger says.<\/p>\n","paginatedContent":[],"excerpt":"<p>The city opened hotel rooms to protect medically data-lazy=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/20210304_MM_DCist_LostSock-7.jpg\" \/><div class=\"slideshow-caption\">Lost Sock\u2019s Takoma cafe is the company\u2019s first brick and mortar location. <span class=\"credits\">Mariah Miranda \/ DCist<\/span><\/div><\/div><div><img alt=\"\" data-lazy=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/20210304_MM_DCist_LostSock-6.jpg\" \/><div class=\"slideshow-caption\">Lost Sock\u2019s Finca Bruhwer natural processed coffee beans come with plum, blackberry, and cacao notes. <span class=\"credits\">Mariah Miranda \/ DCist<\/span><\/div><\/div><div><img alt=\"\" data-lazy=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/20210304_MM_DCist_LostSock-4.jpg\" \/><div class=\"slideshow-caption\">Lovers Plant Studio stocks Lost Sock Cafe with an affordable variety of houseplants to purchase and take home.<span class=\"credits\">Mariah Miranda \/ DCist<\/span><\/div><\/div><div><img alt=\"\" data-lazy=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/20210304_MM_DCist_LostSock-3.jpg\" \/><div class=\"slideshow-caption\">Lost Sock Coffee aims to feature coffees that are bright, complex, and juicy.<span class=\"credits\">Mariah Miranda \/ DCist<\/span><\/div><\/div><div><img alt=\"\" data-lazy=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/20210304_MM_DCist_LostSock-1.jpg\" \/><div class=\"slideshow-caption\">Lost Sock Coffee sells plants from Lovers Plant Studio, a woman-owned plant retail business based in D.C.<span class=\"credits\">Mariah Miranda \/ DCist<\/span><\/div><\/div><\/div>\n<p>\u201cA lost sock is something that you\u2019re looking for in the morning, like a good cup of coffee,\u201d explains Jeff Yerxa, co-founder of Lost Sock Roasters, explaining the name of his company that opened its first caf\u00e9 in Takoma last month.<\/p>\n<p>But the shop doesn\u2019t offer routine caffeine, generally eschewing classic brews full of dark notes and chocolatey tones. \u201cI like the coffees that make you think, \u2018Is this coffee?\u2019\u201d says co-founder Nico Cabrera. \u201cMore natural processed coffees known for acidity, fruitiness, and sweetness.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>For the last five years, Lost Sock Roasters sold their beans at farmers markets, boutique grocers, and to local eateries for their coffee programs. Most of their beans currently come from Latin America and Africa, though they are experimenting with some from Sumatra. There is drip coffee and pour overs available at their cafe, as well as a full slate of espresso drinks. Two cold brews are on hand: an Ethiopian single origin Cabrera says is \u201ca little more fruity and a little more punchy\u201d and another that has a more mainstream flavor profile he describes as \u201cchocolatey, nutty, approachable.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>If a customer wants to discuss the finer tasting notes of any of the coffees, discover the origin story behind the beans, or geek out about the roasting process, the team is happy to talk shop. But they\u2019re not going to force these conversations on anyone. \u201cOne thing we hate is the snobbiness of upscale cafes,\u201d says Yerxa. \u201cThat\u2019s one thing we wanted to avoid. It\u2019s really about meeting the customer where they want.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>As Yerxa and Cabrera were planning the caf\u00e9, they knew they wanted to offer food that cut above coffeehouse stereotypes. They offer half a dozen Argentinian-style empanadas, palm-sized pastries sporting thin crusts baked rich golden brown. They\u2019re made by Cabrera\u2019s parents, who live in Hatboro, Pennsylvania. They formerly owned a Latin American restaurant specializing in Ecuadorian, Peruvian, and Argentinian cuisine, but they left that venture behind to start up the empanada operation, Hungry Moon in Hatboro. Four options are always on hand: steak and cheddar cheese; bacon, egg, and mozzarella; spinach and feta; and barbecued pulled pork. Specials rotate into the mix, such as Buffalo chicken and Argentinian style chicken with olives, onions, and peppers. Hungry Moon also provides pan de yucca, puffy cassava powered cheese breads. And there is a selection of more traditional, locally made pastries from Panorama Bakery.<\/p>\n<p>There are a couple of toasts on hand, built on sourdough and rye breads from Breadfurst. Options are changing regularly, but have included Gruyere with marinated roasted red peppers, and house-made jam (such as blackberry or tomato) with butter and mozzarella. Two sandwiches are on offer: a Cubano with sauerkraut, and prosciutto with manchego cheese. Sometimes Cabrera makes Philly-style tomato pie with focaccia-like crust, a nod to the time he spent growing up in Pennsylvania.<\/p>\n<div class='wamu-slideshow'><div><img alt=\"\" data-lazy=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/20210304_MM_DCist_LostSock-21.jpg\" \/><div class=\"slideshow-caption\">The cafe offers a variety of fresh pastries, sandwiches, empanadas and pan de yuca.<span class=\"credits\">Mariah Miranda \/ DCist<\/span><\/div><\/div><div><img alt=\"\" data-lazy=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/20210304_MM_DCist_LostSock-11.jpg\" \/><div class=\"slideshow-caption\">The menu includes four types of empanadas: pulled pork, bacon egg and cheese, spinach and feta, and Argentinian-style chicken. <span class=\"credits\">Mariah Miranda \/ DCist<\/span><\/div><\/div><div><img alt=\"\" data-lazy=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/20210304_MM_DCist_LostSock-12.jpg\" \/><div class=\"slideshow-caption\">Seasonal toast is available on sourdough or marbled rye with oat yogurt, persimmon, beet gel, and bee pollen. <span class=\"credits\">Mariah Miranda \/ DCist<\/span><\/div><\/div><div><img alt=\"\" data-lazy=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/20210304_MM_DCist_LostSock-14.jpg\" \/><div class=\"slideshow-caption\">Pastries, both sweet and savory, are offered fresh daily. <span class=\"credits\">Mariah Miranda \/ DCist<\/span><\/div><\/div><div><img alt=\"\" data-lazy=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/20210304_MM_DCist_LostSock-20.jpg\" \/><div class=\"slideshow-caption\">Cubano made with ham, Gruyere cheese, pickles, sauerkraut, mustard and garlic aioli.<span class=\"credits\">Mariah Miranda \/ DCist<\/span><\/div><\/div><\/div>\n<p>The picturesque coffeeshop occupies a corner in the historic Takoma Theater building, home to Children\u2019s National Hospital\u2019s pediatric neurology and behavioral health facilities. Smooth concrete floors contrast with red oak counters and accents. Front facing floor to ceiling windows allow lots of light to wash in, powering the verdant array of plants from Lovers Plant Studio. Further d\u00e9cor comes from rotating artworks on loan from the University of Maryland Gallery of Art.<\/p>\n<p>There\u2019s some sweet symbiosis happening in the neighborhood. Lost Sock Roasters opened soon after vegan doughnut shop <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/02\/04\/donut-run-vegan-doughnuts-takoma-first-look\/\">Donut Run<\/a> just up the street. A lot of customers have been coming in for a coffee before they go wait in line for doughnuts, or they swing by with perky pink box full of rounds in search of some caffeine to pair with them. \u201cIt\u2019s a classic combo,\u201d says Cabrera. \u201cYou can\u2019t go wrong.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The duo first toured the space in June 2018, and planned to open at the beginning of last year. They\u2019re glad that timeline didn\u2019t work out given the pandemic\u2019s devastating impact on many businesses. It\u2019s yet another twist in a somewhat unconventional journey to caf\u00e9 ownership.<\/p>\n<p>Cabrera and Yerxa met sophomore year at American University. Though they had different backgrounds, both worked in food and beverage growing up. After college, Yerxa had a side hustle as a barista while working at an international development firm, where he focused on eco-tourism issues, including helping Colombia grow their tourism around the coffee trade. \u201cI saw the whole supply chain of coffee,\u201d he says. \u201cI was drawn to the internationality of it, how many hands are in it.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The pair started experimenting at home as a hobby using a microwave-sized Behmor coffee roaster. \u201cThat got us sucked into this world,\u201d says Cabrera, who was born in Ecuador, and was drawn to the idea of supporting coffee farmers from his home country and elsewhere in Latin America.<\/p>\n<p>Soon realizing that they would need a deeper skill set to roast on a commercial scale, the pair began taking classes with the Specialty Coffee Association. They formed Lost Sock Roasters in 2015, signed a lease for their roastery in Brightwood early the following year, and were roasting later that spring, selling their beans wholesale and at local farmers markets. Their beans are now brewed at Call Your Mother, Baked &amp; Wired, and The Girl &amp; The Vine, and bags of them can be found at Eat Peach Market, Odd Provisions, and Shop Made In DC.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe definitely took a backwards approach,\u201d says Yerxa. \u201cMost people open a caf\u00e9 first.\u201d<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/lostsockroasters.com\/\"><em>Lost Sock Roasters<\/em><\/a><em> is located at 6833 4th\u00a0St. NW. co-owner.","canonical":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/19\/dc-takoma-first-look-lost-sock-roasters-cafe-coffee-shop\/","featured_image":{"url":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/20210304_MM_DCist_LostSock-18-1024x683.jpg","width":1024,"height":683},"image":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2018\/08\/dcist-default-og-image-1.png"}},{"ID":4901643,"guid":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/19\/george-mason-university-janitors-allege-poor-working-conditions\/","title":"Janitors At George Mason Are Alleging Retaliation And Poor Working Conditions","content":"<p>Complaints over working conditions for janitors at George Mason University have led a local service workers union to file four unfair labor practice charges, alleging poor working conditions and retribution for attempts to organize. They&#8217;ve also spurred a movement of university students and staff demanding policy changes.<\/p>\n<p>More than 220 faculty, staff, students, and alumni of the university have signed on to a <a href=\"https:\/\/actionnetwork.org\/petitions\/a-resolution-to-support-workers-employed-by-contractors-at-gmu?source=direct_link\">petition<\/a> supporting the janitors\u2019 right to organize and demanding that the university improve their working conditions. The union, along with student and faculty groups, held a car caravan rally on Thursday to publicize their demands.<\/p>\n<p>The petition urges the university to adopt a \u201cresponsible contractor policy\u201d that would require improved working conditions for contracted workers \u2014 like higher wages, health care benefits, and apprenticeship opportunities. They are also demanding that the university provide janitors with personal protective equipment and ensure that they have access to coronavirus testing through the university.<\/p>\n<p>The service workers union SEIU 32BJ has filed four <a href=\"https:\/\/wtop.com\/fairfax-county\/2020\/08\/labor-complaint-filed-on-behalf-of-george-mason-janitors\/\">complaints<\/a> against L.T. Services, the contractor hired by George Mason for janitorial services, along with two of its subcontractors.\u00a0The union filed its latest charge earlier this month, and two others have already been settled.<\/p>\n<p>The latest allegations from the union say that employers have been &#8220;interrogating and intimidating workers&#8221; for their attempts to organize. In one case, the union says an employer deducted money from a worker&#8217;s paycheck after they participated in &#8220;concerted activity&#8221;\u2014 activities that are supposed to be legally protected against employer retaliation.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/aboutblaw.com\/U0v\">One of the settled complaints,<\/a> filed in January by SEIU 32BJ, alleges that one subcontractor retaliated against workers who have been trying to unionize by \u201csabotaging their work areas, intimidating workers and making false accusations of theft, physically shoving a worker,\u201d and refusing to pay workers on time.<\/p>\n<p>Eugenio Gudiel, a janitor at the university, says a manager threw powder in an area he had already cleaned to claim that he wasn\u2019t doing his work.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cDuring my 20 years here, I have never been treated like this,\u201d he said in a statement distributed by the service workers union SEIU 32BJ.<\/p>\n<p>According to the union, 40 janitors work at George Mason, employed through the contractor L.T. Services and 10 subcontractors. (A spokesperson did not respond to DCist\/WAMU&#8217;s request for comment by press time.)<\/p>\n<p>Two professors who are part of the group urging reform, Timothy Gibson and Bethany L. Letiecq, wrote an <a href=\"https:\/\/www.washingtonpost.com\/opinions\/local-opinions\/george-mason-university-contractor-exploitation-allegations\/2021\/02\/18\/412c8e04-7084-11eb-85fa-e0ccb3660358_story.html?arc404=true\">op-ed<\/a> in the Washington Post last month tying these calls to action to a larger anti-racism and inclusion efforts that are underway at the university.<\/p>\n<p>GMU President Gregory Washington, they wrote, \u201cstated that his vision is to establish GMU \u2018as a national exemplar of anti-racism and inclusive excellence in action.\u2019 To advance this vision, Mason\u2019s racial justice efforts must center on the margins, upholding the rights and dignity of workers who are keeping our campus safe and clean and helping us grow.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>\u201cMany GMU contracted workers \u2014 janitorial staff, food services workers, building tradespeople \u2014 are immigrants,\u201d said the op-ed. \u201cMany are paid low wages and live in precarious circumstances, in overcrowded housing and in fear of detainment, deportation and family separation. They are vulnerable to employment abuses and exploitation.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>In a written statement in February, Washington <a href=\"https:\/\/president.gmu.edu\/news\/2021-02\/message-president-washington-lt-services\">wrote<\/a> that the institution was \u201cactively\u201d seeking a resolution to the \u201ctroubling allegations\u201d about L.T. Services and its subcontractors. In response to a request for comment, a spokesperson for the university directed DCist\/WAMU to Washington&#8217;s February statement.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe university has conducted an initial review of the complaints,\u201d wrote Washington. \u201cAs a result, I have ordered an outside audit of the labor practices of L.T. Services and its subcontractors as they relate to their contract with Mason. The advisory CPA firm Baker Tilly will conduct the audit, and I look forward to learning the results of what I expect will be a thorough, fair, and thoughtful audit.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Washington wrote at the time that the university would not be offering any additional public comment until the outside audit is done.<\/p>\n<p>A statement from the SEIU 32BJ said the risks presented by the coronavirus pandemic have made the working conditions at the university even more dire. The union says Gudiel, for example, was sick with COVID-19 in November.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe essential janitors, who are often single mothers, aren\u2019t highly paid to begin with and do dangerous, life-saving work to disinfect GMU hallways, sinks, bathrooms, and floors during the COVID pandemic,\u201d the union wrote. \u201cEssential janitors are overwhelmingly immigrants who are sickened and dying from COVID-19 at vastly higher rates while being denied any extra compensation.\u201d<\/p>\n","paginatedContent":[],"excerpt":"<p>The service workers union SEIU 32BJ, along with student and faculty groups, held a car caravan rally on Thursday to publicize their demands. When D.C. launched the initiative in 2018, more than a third of the 1,100 lane miles were in \u201cpoor\u201d condition, but DDOT is on track to eliminate those bumpy roads by 2024. (DDOT&#8217;s guide explains how it characterizes road conditions.) In previous years, DDOT has used a vehicle with sensors and lasers to detect just how cracked and corroded roads were.<\/p>\n<p>If your roads are in bad shape, report it by calling or <a href=\"https:\/\/311.dc.gov\/citizen\/home\">registering the complaint to 311<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-4901639\" src=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/Capture.jpg\" alt=\"DDOT\" width=\"1712\" height=\"613\" srcset=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/Capture-300x107.jpg 300w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/Capture-768x275.jpg 768w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/Capture-1024x367.jpg 1024w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/Capture-1500x537.jpg 1500w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/Capture-900x322.jpg 900w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/Capture-600x215.jpg 600w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/Capture-1600x573.jpg 1600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1712px) 100vw, 1712px\" \/><\/p>\n<p>The dashboard only tracks repaving for streets, sidewalks and street markings; the department also handles some multi-use maintenance but does not list that on its website. Man Supports D.C. Statehood","content":"<p>Folks, it happened. D.C.\u2019s biggest ice cream fan, most enthusiastic former Amtrak commuter, and President of the United States supports statehood for the District, per White House press secretary Jen Psaki.<\/p>\n<p>The statement \u2013 the first time since Joe Biden was inaugurated that his team confirmed his position on the subject \u2013 came at a press briefing on Thursday, when a reporter asked Psaki about the fight for D.C. statehood in light of a planned House Oversight committee hearing on Monday.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cDoes he think [statehood] could \u2014 if it passes the House \u2014 does it have a chance in the Senate given the filibuster situation right now, and what would he or the White House say to the critics who suggest that this is designed to be a Democratic Party power grab, just to get a few more seats in the House and the Senate?\u201d the reporter asked.<\/p>\n<p>Psaki almost stuck the landing.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI think he would say that the half a million people who live in D.C. \u2014 am I getting that number right? It\u2019s grown since I left and went to the suburbs \u2014 would argue with that point, and so would he,\u201d she said. \u201cHe believes they deserve representation. That\u2019s why he supports D.C. statehood.\u201d (To quibble a little, D.C. had more than 700,000 residents as of July 2019, even if Jen Psaki has since abandoned ship.)<\/p>\n<p>Biden previously <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/JoeBiden\/status\/1276285377595281408\">expressed<\/a> support for statehood on the campaign trail last summer.<\/p>\n<p>The president has been getting some not-so-subtle hints about the subject since his welcome back to the city from his neighbors in the Wilson Building down Pennsylvania Ave.: D.C. Mayor Muriel Bowser and her administration.<\/p>\n<p>As early as January 6 \u2014 before <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/01\/06\/dc-trump-election-protest\/\">the violent events of that day<\/a> transpired \u2014 Bowser tweeted a statement pushing for a statehood bill within the first 100 days of the Biden presidency.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWashingtonians have waited over 200 years for the representation we deserve as American citizens,\u201d she wrote. \u201cTo paraphrase Dr. King: when any American is denied democracy, our entire nation is denied those voices and those votes.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The Bowser administration did not immediately return a request for comment.<\/p>\n<p>The White House\u2019s endorsement of D.C. statehood on Thursday comes as the so-called \u201cfilibuster situation\u201d plays out in the Senate. With a razor-thin majority in the Senate, Democrats are hamstrung from <a href=\"https:\/\/wamu.org\/story\/21\/01\/07\/dc-statehood-democrats-in-charge\/\">ending debate and voting on legislation<\/a> that requires a 60-vote majority in order to defeat a filibuster from the Republican minority.<\/p>\n<p>A bill to grant D.C. statehood that was introduced in the House last year by D.C. Del. Eleanor Holmes Norton passed 232-180. Earlier this year, a group of Democratic senators introduced its companion bill in the Senate.<\/p>\n<p>Some Democrats support abolishing the filibuster entirely, but others have remained more cautious. In the press briefing on Thursday, <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/sahilkapur\/status\/1372602176116252688\/photo\/1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reporters asked<\/a> White House communications director Kate Bedingfield questions about Biden\u2019s stance on the filibuster issue \u2014 and Bedingfield didn\u2019t rule out Biden supporting a change to the Senate rules.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWhat the president is not going to do&#8230;is to allow progress and allow benefits to the American people to be held hostage in the process,\u201d she said. \u201cHis goal is to ensure that we can get things done for the American people, and he\u2019s open to a discussion about what that looks like.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Only time will tell if it\u2019s all malarkey, or if D.C. will ultimately have to change its license plate slogan.<\/p>\n","paginatedContent":[],"excerpt":"<p>Does anyone have a line from an Irish poet to sum up the moment? ","canonical":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/18\/area-man-supports-d-c-statehood\/","featured_image":{"url":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/48537834776_937b4647d9_k-1024x683.jpg","width":1024,"height":683},"image":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2018\/08\/dcist-default-og-image-1.png"}},{"ID":4901629,"guid":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/18\/maryland-expands-vaccines-over-60\/","title":"Maryland Expands Vaccine Eligibility To Residents Over 60, All Adults To Be Eligible By April 27","content":"<p>Maryland Gov. Larry Hogan announced Thursday that the state will move into Phase 2A of its vaccine rollout next Tuesday, opening eligibility to all residents over 60.<\/p>\n<p>Starting Thursday, residents 60 and older can pre-register for their <a href=\"https:\/\/coronavirus.maryland.gov\/pages\/vaccine#locator\">appointment online<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>The state will move into Phase 2B on March 30, according to Hogan, expanding vaccine eligibility to residents ages 16 and older with underlying medical conditions. Two weeks later on April 13, the state will move into its final Phase 2 stage, vaccinating all residents 55 and older, and essential workers in industries like construction, food services, utilities, transportation, and financial services. All Marylanders over 16 will be eligible no later than April 27, according to Hogan, who said the state&#8217;s federal allotment of doses will be increasing over the coming weeks and months.<\/p>\n<p>Still, Hogan reminded residents that becoming eligible for a vaccine does not guarantee an immediate appointment.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Supply will be ramping up to meet all of the demand, but to be clear, we do expect that demand will continue to outpace the supply for at least the next several weeks,&#8221; Hogan said during a press conference Thursday.<\/p>\n<p>Regionally, Prince George&#8217;s and Montgomery counties are still working to vaccinate residents in Phases 1A, 1B, and 1C \u2014 including residents over 65, and essential workers like grocery store workers, postal service workers, and teachers. According to the state&#8217;s <a href=\"https:\/\/coronavirus.maryland.gov\/#Vaccine\">vaccine data<\/a>, about 14% of Prince George&#8217;s County residents have received at least one dose of the vaccine, while 22% of Montgomery County residents have received a first dose. Spokespeople for both jurisdictions did not immediately respond when DCist asked if the counties planned to follow Hogan&#8217;s statewide directive.<\/p>\n<p>Exactly one year after the state reported its first resident death from the coronavirus, Hogan announced on Thursday a brighter milestone \u2014 the state has administered 2 million vaccine doses (1 million of those in the past 27 days), reaching 25% of the the state&#8217;s total population, and 65% of all residents 65 and older.<\/p>\n<p>Still,<a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/18\/governments-community-groups-address-racial-disparities-vaccine-dc-md-va\/\"> access gaps persist<\/a> \u2014 despite making up 30% of Maryland&#8217;s population, Black residents account for only 15% of first doses. Hispanic residents constitute just 6% of Maryland&#8217;s overall doses, while they make up 11% of the state&#8217;s total population.<\/p>\n<p>In an effort to correct the large disparities, Hogan announced several initiatives aimed at bringing more vaccines to residents in underserved areas on Thursday. In partnership with the state&#8217;s Vaccine Equity Task Force, Maryland is dedicating $12 million to bolster vaccine distribution and collaboration between hospitals and local health departments, including investing in more mobile vaccination vans and community-based vaccination clinics. The state has also selected 37 primary care officers that will begin administering vaccines to patients in underserved areas, but Hogan did not immediately disclose where these offices would be.<\/p>\n","paginatedContent":[],"excerpt":"<p>As of Thursday, the state has administered 2 million vaccines. <\/p>\n","permalink":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/18\/maryland-expands-vaccines-over-60\/","currentSlug":"maryland-expands-vaccines-over-60","created":"2021-03-18T15:22:49","modified":"2021-03-18T15:22:49","time":"Mar 18","timestamp":1616080969,"timestampGMT":1616095369,"imageData":{"caption":"<p>Maryland Gov.
