These guys are moving so quickly,&#8221; Ludwig says while standing over her folding bike and balancing a piece of white cardboard on a sidewalk post just next to the fence.<\/p>\n<p>The removal of the razor wire comes as the U.S. Capitol Police informed the\u00a0Acting House Sergeant at Arms that\u00a0\u201cthere does not exist a known, credible threat against Congress or the Capitol Complex that warrants the temporary security fencing.&#8221; <a href=\"https:\/\/wjla.com\/news\/local\/capitol-police-to-remove-outer-permiter-fencing-around-us-capitol-complex-over-weekend\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Multiple news outlets<\/a> reported Friday evening that Constitution Avenue and Independence Avenue would\u00a0 re-open to traffic by Monday. Earlier this week Capitol Police said they were improving access to the U.S. Capitol.<\/p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\" lang=\"en\">Barbed wire on the black Capitol fences is being removed today <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/wamu885?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@wamu885<\/a> <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/DCist?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@DCist<\/a> <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/QyQPZXAHyJ\">pic.twitter.com\/QyQPZXAHyJ<\/a><\/p>\n<p>\u2014 Dominique Maria Bonessi (@dbonessi) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/dbonessi\/status\/1373354862658916356?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 20, 2021<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The USCP has already modified fencing along 3rd St., NW, Louisiana Ave., NW, and Washington Ave., SW to help drivers and pedestrians. For security reasons, we will not provide a detailed timeline of specific, future changes,&#8221; Capitol Police officials <a href=\"https:\/\/www.uscp.gov\/media-center\/press-releases\/uscp-statement-security-changes-us-capitol\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">wrote in a statement<\/a>.<\/p>\n<div id=\"attachment_4901857\" style=\"width: 3010px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><img class=\"size-full wp-image-4901857\" src=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"3000\" height=\"2250\" srcset=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-2-300x225.jpg 300w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-2-768x576.jpg 768w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-2-1024x768.jpg 1024w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-2-1500x1125.jpg 1500w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-2-900x675.jpg 900w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-2-600x450.jpg 600w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-2-1600x1200.jpg 1600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 3000px) 100vw, 3000px\" \/><p class=\"wp-caption-text\"><span>Katherine Ludwig paints as a group of contractors remove razor wire from the black fence around the Capitol.<\/span><span class=\"credits\">WAMU\/DCist \/ Dominique Maria Bonessi<\/span><\/p><\/div>\n<p>Like many in the Capitol Hill community Saturday afternoon, Ludwig says she&#8217;s happy to see the bared wire coming down. She moved to the District from Brooklyn, NY in September to paint the monuments and buildings.\u00a0She watched and painted as the fences went up around the Capitol.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;It&#8217;s very moving to see the people&#8217;s house sequestered, closed in by razor wire,&#8221; Ludwig says as she continues to paint a flatbed truck full of miles of curled razor wire. &#8220;This gorgeous city turned into the insane-looking city by, but it&#8217;s coming back again.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Ludwig she says she&#8217;s excited to start painting other things \u2014like the cherry blossoms \u2014 soon.<\/p>\n<p>Along D Street SE across from the black fencing Ally, who wouldn&#8217;t give her last name, and her husband, are out for a walk to see if they can get to the National Mall from their home in Capitol Heights without having to walk around the fencing.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;It&#8217;s just a sad reminder of where things are and it&#8217;d be nice to start healing and moving past the physical reminders of that,&#8221; she says.<\/p>\n<p>Ally says they bought their house on Capitol Hill in July because they &#8220;loved the neighborhood feeling, we wanted to raise a family here, and live in a quiet street, good schools, get to know your neighbors, and yeah, hard during COVID, harder with everything else going on.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Ally says she&#8217;s hoping that once the fences are down, a bit of normalcy can return to life on Capitol Hill.<\/p>\n<p>Further up D St., Julie and DeAngelo Mohead from Dallas, TX are trying to take their four kids to see the Capitol steps.\u00a0 This DCist reporter informed them of the situation.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We did the bus tour today and, of course, we walked around all the monuments, but the bus tour didn&#8217;t even go around the Capitol. I&#8217;m assuming because of all the fences,&#8221; said Julie Mohead.<\/p>\n<p>The family returns to Texas Monday.<\/p>\n<div id=\"attachment_4901861\" style=\"width: 3010px\" class=\"wp-caption alignleft\"><img class=\"size-full wp-image-4901861\" src=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-5.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"3000\" height=\"2250\" srcset=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-5-300x225.jpg 300w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-5-768x576.jpg 768w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-5-1024x768.jpg 1024w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-5-1500x1125.jpg 1500w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-5-900x675.jpg 900w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-5-600x450.jpg 600w, https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-5-1600x1200.jpg 1600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 3000px) 100vw, 3000px\" \/><p class=\"wp-caption-text\"><span>Elaine Wilson, a painter from Silver Spring, has been working on this painting for weeks.<\/span><span class=\"credits\">WAMU\/DCist \/ Dominique Maria Bonessi<\/span><\/p><\/div>\n<p>Another local artist, Elaine Wilson from Silver Spring, stands at an easel on the corner of D St. and New Jersey Ave. SE.\u00a0Wilson has been working on her painting of the Capitol with the fencing around it for a couple of weeks.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;I&#8217;m really ready for [the fence] to be taken down, and if I don&#8217;t end up making any paintings of it it&#8217;s probably good for the city,&#8221; Wilson chuckles. &#8220;I&#8217;d rather we take the fence down than me make a bunch of paintings.&#8221;<\/p>\n","paginatedContent":[],"excerpt":"<p>Capitol Police say with no &#8220;credible threat,&#8221; warranted.","canonical":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/20\/ive-got-to-paint-fast-local-residents-watch-as-capitol-fence-razor-wire-comes-down\/","featured_image":{"url":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/FENCE-1-1024x768.jpg","width":1024,"height":768},"image":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2018\/08\/dcist-default-og-image-1.png"},"provider":{"term_id":41688,"name":"WAMU","slug":"wamu","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":41688,"taxonomy":"wamu_provider","description":"","parent":0,"count":832,"filter":"raw","permalink":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/provider\/wamu\/","nameOverride":false}},{"ID":4901843,"guid":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/20\/new-nonprofit-wants-to-educate-the-districts-business-community-about-statehood\/","title":"New Nonprofit Wants To Educate The District\u2019s Business Community About Statehood","content":"<p>A new organization in the District is working to educate policymakers and the business community on what it would mean to be the 51st state.<\/p>\n<p>Federal City Council, a civic organization, launched their nonprofit, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.statehoodresearchdc.org\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Statehood Research DC<\/a>, over the weekend as the U.S House plans to hold a hearing on D.C. statehood Monday. The nonprofit\u2019s mission is to conduct research and educate policymakers and business owners about what changes statehood would bring to the District.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThere\u2019s a lot of interest in the business community for how [statehood] would work and how it\u2019s going to affect the finances and the economy of the region,\u201d Gregory McCarthy, chair of the nonprofit and a 30-plus year resident of the District, told WAMU\/DCist.<\/p>\n<p>In the past few months, McCarthy says, there have been two instances when the lack of statehood have been detrimental to the city\u2019s fiscal and economic prospects. The first was when the District was <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/20\/03\/25\/a-recovery-bill-moving-through-the-senate-would-give-d-c-half-as-much-funding-as-other-states\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">initially cut out of $755 million in federal COVID-19 relief stimulus money<\/a> because of its designation as a territory. That matter was later resolved. And the second was during the attack on the U.S. Capitol in early January. &#8220;The mayor\u2019s ability to protect the city and the federal Capital was shortchanged because she didn\u2019t have the power of being a governor,\u201d McCarthy said.<\/p>\n<p>McCarthy says that while recent arguments for statehood have centered around social justice, \u201cas business leaders we think it\u2019s incumbent upon us to step up and now join the justice community in saying it\u2019s about time.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>On Friday, the organization published their first research project by <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/02\/01\/the-historian-behind-chocolate-city-wants-you-to-know-how-the-black-power-movement-reshaped-d-c\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">George Derek Musgrove and Chris Myers Asch<\/a>, two of the city\u2019s leading historians and co-authors of <em>Chocolate City: A History of Race and Democracy in the Nation\u2019s Capital<\/em>. <a href=\"https:\/\/assets.website-files.com\/5df7f915fcb12b538aa0494f\/60541fb1af8047a0fde84ad7_Democracy%20Deferred.March.2021.pdf\">The report<\/a>\u00a0looks at the intersection of the challenge of DC statehood and voting rights for Black people and all women.<\/p>\n<p>It had three major takeaways: The first was that the <a href=\"https:\/\/wamu.org\/story\/20\/09\/29\/51st-what-hamilton-got-wrong-about-d-c\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">country\u2019s founding fathers<\/a> never \u201creconciled the tension between the revolutionary imperative for \u2018no taxation without representation\u2019 and the federal government\u2019s need for \u2018exclusive legislation\u2019 regarding the seat of government.\u201d The second finding is that following reconstruction in 1874 the District\u2019s Black and white residents lost all voting rights. The report says this action \u201cplayed a significant role in defeating all attempts to win home rule and congressional representation as segregationists successfully derailed efforts to return suffrage to District residents.\u201d Finally, throughout the 1960s and 70s, the report says, activists managed to win a series of victories:\u00a0 gaining the right to vote in presidential elections, a local government, and a non-voting member of the U.S. House.<\/p>\n<p>Statehood Research DC said <a href=\"https:\/\/www.federalcitycouncil.org\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/SRDC-Press-Release.3.19.21.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">in a statement<\/a> that they hope the report highlights these points during Monday\u2019s House hearing \u2014 \u201cespecially the role of race in depriving DC residents of local legislative independence and voting representation in Congress.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The organization also hopes to conduct other research around the wide array of legal issues related to statehood, such as the criminal justice system and economic competitiveness in the region.<\/p>\n<p>D.C. Delegate Eleanor Holmes Norton<a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/01\/04\/eleanor-holmes-norton-dc-statehood-congress\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> reintroduced the statehood bill<\/a> in January with 202 cosponsors. Later that month a <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/01\/27\/senate-democrats-dc-statehood-bill\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">similar measure was introduced in the U.S. Senate<\/a> with a record number of cosponsors, 38, since it was first introduced in 2013. Last week, <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/18\/area-man-supports-d-c-statehood\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">President Joe Biden confirmed his support<\/a> for statehood.<\/p>\n<p>Norton will be holding a press conference Monday morning prior to the U.S. House hearing.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cI am confident Monday will make the case for granting the residents of the nation\u2019s capital, who have worked for 220 years for this imprimatur, all the elements and the full meaning of citizenship. Statehood for the District of Columbia will give real meaning to the nation\u2019s oldest slogan: \u2018no taxation without representation.\u2019 Statehood is about giving the people of the District of Columbia a voice and a say in their own government,\u201d Norton wrote <a href=\"https:\/\/norton.house.gov\/media-center\/press-releases\/norton-looking-forward-to-press-conference-ahead-of-dc-statehood-hearing\">in a statement.<\/a><\/p>\n","paginatedContent":[],"excerpt":"<p>U.S. House plans to take up statehood measure in hearing on | DCist","description":"\"And that's how I met Jack Kennedy.\u201d","canonical":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/19\/overheard-in-dc-march-19\/","featured_image":{"url":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2021\/03\/51037476338_ebb46b7018_k-1024x683.jpg","width":1024,"height":683},"image":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/sites\/3\/2018\/08\/dcist-default-og-image-1.png"}},{"ID":4901806,"guid":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/19\/wanna-bet-on-the-home-team-in-march-madness-it-may-require-crossing-the-potomac-river\/","title":"Wanna Bet On The Home Team In March Madness? It May Require Crossing The Potomac River","content":"<p>If you passionately believe that Georgetown&#8217;s going to go all the way in this year&#8217;s March Madness, you can now legally put some money on it \u2014 but it will take a trip across the Key Bridge to get it done.<\/p>\n<p>Of the\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/www.legalsportsbetting.com\/states-with-legal-sports-betting\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">24 states have legalized sports betting<\/a> in recent years, D.C. and Virginia are among the handful that have imposed a very specific prohibition on it when it comes to college sports \u2014 there&#8217;s absolutely no betting on any in-state schools if you&#8217;re using any of the legal wagering apps or brick-and-mortar sportsbooks.<\/p>\n<p>And that could well prove an unexpected inconvenience in the area, where D.C. and Virginia have a combined five teams in the men&#8217;s tournament \u2014 Georgetown, Virginia, Liberty, Norfolk State, and VCU. (Virginia Tech lost to Florida earlier this afternoon.)<\/p>\n<p>In D.C., true blue-blooded Hoyas fans will have to cross into Virginia to legally bet on their team, just as a Fairfax County resident who thinks that Norfolk State will upend everyone&#8217;s expectations will have to travel into D.C. to put some money on it. (Sports betting apps are geo-located, so where you are standing when you place a bet matters.)<\/p>\n<p>The restrictions stem from a <a href=\"https:\/\/sportshandle.com\/why-ban-college-sports-betting\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">concern among some university officials and elected leaders<\/a> that while sports betting can bring in loads of revenue for local coffers, it could also serve to corrupt non-professional sports and athletes.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The monetization of student athletes through legalized sports wagering will expose collegiate athletes and their community of classmates, friends, family, co-workers, and neighbors to the pressures of the gambling industry,&#8221; wrote John Cavanaugh, then president of the Consortium of Universities of the Washington Metropolitan Area, to D.C. Lottery officials in 2019 as they were <a href=\"https:\/\/wamu.org\/story\/19\/05\/15\/should-local-sports-fans-be-allowed-to-place-legal-bets-on-college-teams-d-c-wants-to-say-no\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">developing the rules for sports betting in the city<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Virginia followed suit when it <a href=\"https:\/\/wamu.org\/story\/19\/05\/15\/should-local-sports-fans-be-allowed-to-place-legal-bets-on-college-teams-d-c-wants-to-say-no\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">crafted its own sports betting program<\/a>, which <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/01\/22\/sports-betting-app-launches-virginia\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">launched earlier this year<\/a>. In Maryland, voters approved sports betting in a Nov. 2020 referendum, and a bill implementing the program <a href=\"https:\/\/baltimore.cbslocal.com\/2021\/03\/11\/maryland-house-approves-sports-betting-implementation-bill\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">cleared the House of Delegates earlier this month<\/a> \u2014 without a specific prohibition on betting on in-state colleges and universities.<\/p>\n<p>For some D.C. sports fans, there&#8217;s an additional challenge: there&#8217;s <a href=\"https:\/\/washingtoncitypaper.com\/article\/511891\/even-with-legal-betting-the-march-madness-experience-is-still-not-a-reality-in-d-c\/\">only one<\/a> brick-and-mortar sportsbook currently operating in town \u2014 <a href=\"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/20\/08\/02\/d-c-s-first-sportsbook-is-now-open-to-take-bets\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">William Hill at Capital One Arena<\/a> \u2014 and only one app that works citywide, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.dclotterysportsbetting.com\/playing-sports-betting\/about-gambetdc\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">GambetDC<\/a>, which was developed by the D.C. Lottery. (It launched last year to <a href=\"https:\/\/www.washingtonpost.com\/local\/dc-politics\/2020\/09\/15\/0997522c-f757-11ea-a275-1a2c2d36e1f1_story.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">mixed reactions<\/a>; it currently only 1.5 out of 5 stars in Apple&#8217;s App Store.)<\/p>\n<p>Virginia officials, on the other hand, decided to allow a number of private sports betting apps to operate, including FanDuel, DraftKings, BetMGM, and WynnBet. Maryland is likely to follow suit.<\/p>\n","paginatedContent":[],"excerpt":"<p>Both D.C. and Virginia, where sports betting is legal, prohibit wagering in in-state colleges and universities, even if they are playing somewhere else.<\/p>\n","permalink":"https:\/\/dcist.com\/story\/21\/03\/19\/wanna-bet-on-the-home-team-in-march-madness-it-may-require-crossing-the-potomac-river\/","currentSlug":"wanna-bet-on-the-home-team-in-march-madness-it-may-require-crossing-the-potomac-river","created":"2021-03-19T15:59:43","modified":"2021-03-19T15:59:43","time":"Mar
